			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Seven Years' War</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the European mid-18th-century war. For other wars of the same name, see <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Seven Years' War (disambiguation)">Seven Years' War (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<table class="mw-stack mobile-float-reset" role="presentation" style="float:right;clear:right;background:transparent;margin:0;padding:0">
<tr>
<td>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="border-spacing:2px;;width:315px">
<tr>
<th class="summary" colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Seven Years' War</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.5em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Seven Years' War Collage.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg/300px-Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg" width="300" height="300" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg/450px-Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg/600px-Seven_Years%27_War_Collage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2400" /></a><br />
Clockwise from top left: the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> (23 June 1757); the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carillon" title="Battle of Carillon">Battle of Carillon</a> (6–8 July 1758); the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zorndorf" title="Battle of Zorndorf">Battle of Zorndorf</a> (25 August 1758); the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kunersdorf" title="Battle of Kunersdorf">Battle of Kunersdorf</a> (12 August 1759).</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2">
<table style="width:100%;margin:0;padding:0;border:0">
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>17&#160;May&#160;1756&#160;– 15&#160;February&#160;1763 <span style="display:none">(<span class="dtstart">1756-05-17</span>&#160;– <span class="dtend">1763-02-15</span>)</span><br />
(6&#160;years, 8&#160;months, 4&#160;weeks and 1&#160;day)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location"><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td>
<p>Anglo-Prusso-Portuguese Coalition victory</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint_Petersburg_(1762)" title="Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1762)">Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1762)</a></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hamburg_(1762)" title="Treaty of Hamburg (1762)">Treaty of Hamburg (1762)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg (1763)</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Territorial<br />
changes</th>
<td>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo_ante_bellum" title="Status quo ante bellum">Status quo ante bellum</a></i> in Europe. Transfer of colonial possessions between Great Britain, France, Spain, and Portugal.</p>
<ul>
<li>France cedes its possessions east of the Mississippi River, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> (except <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre_and_Miquelon" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Pierre and Miquelon">Saint-Pierre and Miquelon</a>), the island of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Circars" title="Northern Circars">Northern Circars</a> in India to Great Britain.</li>
<li>France cedes <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and its territory west of the Mississippi River to Spain.</li>
<li>Spain cedes <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a> to Great Britain.</li>
<li>Four "neutral" Caribbean islands divided between Britain (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent (island)">St. Vincent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>) and France (<a href="/wiki/St._Lucia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a>)</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia"><img alt="Kingdom of Prussia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Kingdom_of_Prussia_%281750-1801%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> 180,000 dead<br />
80,000 deserted<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785-1">[1]</a></sup><br />
33,000 civilians killed<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeelman2012524_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeelman2012524-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France"><img alt="Kingdom of France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/23px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/35px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/45px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <b>350,000</b><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">French losses</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;">
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><b>Total losses</b>
<ul>
<li>200,000 dead, wounded or missing</li>
<li>80,000 captured</li>
<li>70,000 deserted</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy"><img alt="Habsburg Monarchy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg/23px-Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg/35px-Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg/45px-Banner_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor_%28after_1400%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a></span> <b>373,588</b><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter201785-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">Austrian losses</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;">
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><b>Total losses</b>

<li>19,592 missing</li>
<li>17,388 disabled</li>
<li>70,000 slightly wounded</li>
<li>78,360 captured</li>
<li>62,222 deserted</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<p>The <b>Seven Years' War</b> was a <a href="/wiki/Global_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Global conflict">global conflict</a> fought between 1756 and 1763. It involved every European <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> of the time and spanned five continents, affecting Europe, the Americas, West Africa, India, and the Philippines. The conflict split Europe into two coalitions, led by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Brunswick-L%C3%BCneburg" title="Electorate of Brunswick-Lüneburg">Hanover</a>, and other small German states) on one side and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austrian-led Holy Roman Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbon Spain">Bourbon Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>) on the other. Meanwhile, in India, the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, with the support of the French, tried to crush a British attempt to conquer <a href="/wiki/Nawabs_of_Bengal_and_Murshidabad" title="Nawabs of Bengal and Murshidabad">Bengal</a>.</p>
<p>Although Anglo-French skirmishes over their American colonies had begun with what became the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> in 1754, the large-scale conflict that drew in most of the European powers was centered on Austria's desire to recover <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> from the Prussians. Seeing the opportunity to curtail Britain's and Prussia's ever-growing might, France and Austria put aside their <a href="/wiki/French%E2%80%93Habsburg_relations" title="French–Habsburg relations">ancient rivalry</a> to form a grand coalition of their own, bringing most of the other European powers to their side. Faced with this sudden turn of events, Britain aligned itself with Prussia, in a series of political manoeuvres known as the <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">Diplomatic Revolution</a>. However, French efforts ended in failure when the Anglo-Prussian coalition prevailed, and Britain's rise as among the world's <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">predominant powers</a> destroyed France's supremacy in Europe, thus altering the <a href="/wiki/European_balance_of_power" title="European balance of power">European balance of power</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Conflict between Great Britain and France broke out in 1754–1756 when the British attacked disputed French positions in North America, starting with a British ambush of a small French force at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen" title="Battle of Jumonville Glen">Battle of Jumonville Glen</a> on 28 May 1754, and extended across the colonial boundaries and the seizure of hundreds of French merchant ships at sea. Meanwhile, rising power Prussia was struggling with <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austria</a> for dominance within and outside the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> in central Europe. In 1756, the major powers "<a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">switched partners</a>".</p>
<p>Realizing that war was imminent, Prussia preemptively struck <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Saxony</a> and quickly <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pirna" title="Siege of Pirna">overran</a> it. The result caused uproar across Europe. Because of Austria's <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles_(1756)" title="Treaty of Versailles (1756)">alliance with France</a> to recapture <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, which had been lost in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>, Prussia formed an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Prussian_alliance_(1756)" title="Anglo-Prussian alliance (1756)">alliance with Britain</a>. Reluctantly, by following the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">imperial diet</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Reichskrieg" title="Reichskrieg">declared war on Prussia</a> on 17 January 1757, most of the states of the empire joined Austria's cause. The Anglo-Prussian alliance was joined by smaller <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_in_the_Holy_Roman_Empire" title="List of states in the Holy Roman Empire">German states</a> (especially the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Hanover" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of Hanover">Electorate of Hanover</a>). <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Empire" title="Swedish Empire">Sweden</a>, seeking to re-gain Pomerania (most of which had been lost to Prussia in previous wars) joined the coalition, seeing its chance when virtually all of Europe opposed Prussia. <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbon Spain">Spain</a>, bound by the <a href="/wiki/Pacte_de_Famille" title="Pacte de Famille">Pacte de Famille</a>, intervened on behalf of France and together they launched an utterly unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Spanish_invasion_of_Portugal_(1762)" title="Spanish invasion of Portugal (1762)">invasion of Portugal</a> in 1762. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> was originally aligned with Austria, fearing Prussia's ambition on the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>, but switched sides upon the succession of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">Peter III</a> in 1762.</p>
<p>Many middle and small powers in Europe, unlike in the previous wars, tried to steer clear away from the escalating conflict, even though they had interests in the conflict or with the belligerents, like <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Denmark–Norway</a>. <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Denmark–Norway</a> was, however, close to being dragged into the war on France's side when <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">Peter III</a> became Russian emperor and switched sides; Dano-Norwegian and Russian armies were close to ending up in battle, but the Russian emperor was deposed before war formally broke out. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, a long-time British ally, kept its neutrality intact, fearing the odds against Britain and Prussia fighting the great powers of Europe, and even <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chinsurah" title="Battle of Chinsurah">tried to prevent</a> Britain's domination in India. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Sicily</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Savoy</a>, although sided with the Franco-Spanish alliance, declined to join the coalition under fear of British naval power. The taxation needed for war caused the Russian people considerable hardship, being added to the taxation of salt and alcohol begun by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia" title="Elizabeth of Russia">Empress Elizabeth</a> in 1759 to complete her addition to the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">Winter Palace</a>. Like Sweden, Russia concluded a separate peace with Prussia.</p>
<p>The war ended with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> between France, Spain and Great Britain and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a> between Saxony, Austria and Prussia, in 1763.</p>
<p>The war was successful for Great Britain, which gained the bulk of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> in North America, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>, some individual <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> islands in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, the colony of <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> on the West African coast, and superiority over the French trading outposts on the Indian subcontinent. The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American tribes</a> were excluded from the settlement; a subsequent conflict, known as <a href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_War" title="Pontiac's War">Pontiac's War</a>, was also unsuccessful in returning them to their pre-war status. In Europe, the war began disastrously for Prussia, but a combination of good luck and successful strategy saw King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> manage to retrieve the Prussian position and retain the <i><a href="/wiki/Status_quo_ante_bellum" title="Status quo ante bellum">status quo ante bellum</a></i>. Prussia emerged as a new European great power. Although Austria failed to retrieve the territory of Silesia from Prussia (its original goal) its military prowess was also noted by the other powers. The involvement of Portugal, Spain and Sweden did not return them to their former status as great powers. France was deprived of many of its colonies and had saddled itself with heavy war debts that its inefficient financial system could barely handle. Spain lost Florida but gained <a href="/wiki/French_Louisiana" title="French Louisiana">French Louisiana</a> and regained control of its colonies, e.g., <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cuba" title="History of Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_the_Philippines" title="Captaincy General of the Philippines">the Philippines</a>, which had been captured by the British during the war. France and Spain avenged their defeat during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, with hopes of destroying Britain's dominance once and for all.</p>
<p>The Seven Years' War was perhaps the first true world war, having taken place almost 160 years before <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and influenced many major events later around the globe. The war restructured not only the European political order, but also affected events all around the world, paving the way for the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Pax_britannica" class="mw-redirect" title="Pax britannica">later British world supremacy</a> in the 19th century, the rise of Prussia in Germany, the beginning of <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">tensions in British North America</a>, as well as a clear sign of <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">France's eventual turmoil</a>. It was characterized in Europe by sieges and the arson of towns as well as open battles with heavy losses.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">Nomenclature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Nomenclature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the historiography of some countries, the war is named after combatants in its respective theatres. In the present-day United States — at the time, the southern English-speaking British colonies in North America — the conflict is known as the <b><a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a></b> (1754–1763). In English-speaking Canada — the balance of Britain's former North American colonies — it is called the <b>Seven Years' War</b> (1754–1763). In French-speaking Canada, it is known as <i>La guerre de la Conquête</i> (the <b>War of the Conquest</b>). Swedish historiography uses the name <i>Pommerska kriget</i> (<b><a href="/wiki/Pomeranian_War" title="Pomeranian War">Pomeranian War</a></b>), as the Sweden–Prussian involvement in 1757–1762 was limited to <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Pomerania" title="Swedish Pomerania">Pomerania</a> in northern central Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-fuessel7_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fuessel7-4">[4]</a></sup> The <b><a href="/wiki/Third_Silesian_War" title="Third Silesian War">Third Silesian War</a></b> involved Prussia and Austria (1756–1763). On the Indian subcontinent, the conflict is called the <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_Wars" title="Carnatic Wars"><b>Third Carnatic War</b></a> (1757–1763).</p>
<p>The war has been described as the first "<a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">world war</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-Bowen_1998_7_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bowen_1998_7-5">[5]</a></sup> although this label was also given to various earlier conflicts like the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>, and to later conflicts like the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. The term "<a href="/wiki/Second_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Second Hundred Years' War">Second Hundred Years' War</a>" has been used in order to describe the almost continuous level of worldwide conflict between France and Great Britain during the entire 18th century, reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a> of the 14th and 15th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">Diplomatic Revolution</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Europe">In Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: In Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>

</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SevenYearsWar.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/SevenYearsWar.png/340px-SevenYearsWar.png" width="340" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/SevenYearsWar.png/510px-SevenYearsWar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/SevenYearsWar.png/680px-SevenYearsWar.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SevenYearsWar.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
All the participants of the Seven Years' War
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4D6DF3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Great Britain, Prussia, Portugal, with allies</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #22B14C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;France, Spain, Austria, Russia, Sweden with allies</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> which lasted from 1740 to 1748, King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick II of Prussia">Frederick&#160;II of Prussia</a>, known as Frederick the Great, seized the prosperous province of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> from Austria. Empress <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Theresa of Austria">Maria Theresa of Austria</a> had signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a> in 1748 in order to gain time to rebuild her military forces and forge new alliances.</p>
<p>The War of the Austrian Succession had seen the belligerents aligned on a time-honoured basis. France’s traditional enemies, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austria</a>, had coalesced just as they had done against Louis XIV. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>, the leading anti-Austrian state in Germany, had been supported by France. Neither group, however, found much reason to be satisfied with its partnership: British subsidies to Austria produced nothing of much help to the British, while the British military effort had not saved Silesia for Austria. Prussia, having secured Silesia, came to terms with Austria in disregard of French interests. Even so, France concluded a defensive alliance with Prussia in 1747, and the maintenance of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Austrian_Alliance" title="Anglo-Austrian Alliance">Anglo-Austrian alignment</a> after 1748 was deemed essential by the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pelham-Holles,_1st_Duke_of_Newcastle" title="Thomas Pelham-Holles, 1st Duke of Newcastle">Duke of Newcastle</a>, British secretary of state in the ministry of his brother <a href="/wiki/Henry_Pelham" title="Henry Pelham">Henry Pelham</a>. The collapse of that system and the aligning of France with Austria and of Great Britain with Prussia constituted what is known as the "<a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic revolution">diplomatic revolution</a>" or the "reversal of alliances."</p>
<p>In 1756 Austria was making military preparations for war with Prussia and pursuing an alliance with Russia for this purpose. On 2 June 1746, Austria and Russia concluded a defensive alliance that covered their own territory and <a href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth">Poland</a> against attack by Prussia or the Ottoman Empire. They also agreed to a secret clause that promised the restoration of Silesia and the countship of Glatz (now <a href="/wiki/K%C5%82odzko" title="Kłodzko">Kłodzko</a>, Poland) to Austria in the event of hostilities with Prussia. Their real desire, however, was to destroy Frederick’s power altogether, reducing his sway to his electorate of Brandenburg and giving <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a> to Poland, an exchange that would be accompanied by the cession of the Polish <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Courland">Duchy of Courland</a> to Russia. <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Bestuzhev-Ryumin" title="Alexey Bestuzhev-Ryumin">Alexey Bestuzhev-Ryumin</a>, grand chancellor of Russia under <a href="/wiki/Empress_Elizabeth_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Empress Elizabeth of Russia">Empress Elizabeth</a>, was hostile to both France and Prussia, but he could not persuade Austrian statesman <a href="/wiki/Wenzel_Anton_von_Kaunitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Wenzel Anton von Kaunitz">Wenzel Anton von Kaunitz</a> to commit to offensive designs against Prussia so long as Prussia was able to rely on French support.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1748-1766_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/280px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png" width="280" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/420px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Europe_1748-1766_en.png/560px-Europe_1748-1766_en.png 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2761" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_1748-1766_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Europe in the years after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a> in 1748</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Hanoverian king <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II of Great Britain</a> was passionately devoted to his family's continental holdings, but his commitments in Germany were counterbalanced by the demands of the British colonies overseas. If war against France for colonial expansion was to be resumed, then Hanover had to be secured against Franco-Prussian attack. France was very much interested in colonial expansion and was willing to exploit the vulnerability of Hanover in war against Great Britain, but it had no desire to divert forces to central Europe for Prussia's interest.</p>
<p>French policy was, moreover, complicated by the existence of the <i><a href="/wiki/Secret_du_Roi" title="Secret du Roi">Secret du Roi</a></i>—a system of private diplomacy conducted by King Louis XV. Unbeknownst to his foreign minister, Louis had established a network of agents throughout Europe with the goal of pursuing personal political objectives that were often at odds with France’s publicly stated policies. Louis’s goals for <i>le Secret du roi</i> included the Polish crown for his kinsman <a href="/wiki/Louis_Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Bourbon,_prince_de_Conti" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis François de Bourbon, prince de Conti">Louis François de Bourbon, prince de Conti</a>, and the maintenance of Poland, Sweden, and Turkey as French client states in opposition to Russian and Austrian interests.</p>
<p>Frederick saw <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Saxony" title="Electorate of Saxony">Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prussia" title="Royal Prussia">Polish west Prussia</a> as potential fields for expansion but could not expect French support if he started an aggressive war for them. If he joined the French against the British in the hope of annexing Hanover, he might fall victim to an Austro-Russian attack. The hereditary elector of Saxony, <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus III">Augustus III</a>, was also elective King of Poland as Augustus III, but the two territories were physically separated by Brandenburg and Silesia. Neither state could pose as a great power. Saxony was merely a buffer between Prussia and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian Bohemia">Austrian Bohemia</a>, whereas Poland, despite its union with the ancient lands of Lithuania, was prey to pro-French and pro-Russian factions. A Prussian scheme for compensating Frederick Augustus with Bohemia in exchange for Saxony obviously presupposed further spoliation of Austria.</p>
<p>In the attempt to satisfy Austria at the time, Britain gave their electoral vote in Hanover for the candidacy of Maria Theresa's son, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a>, as the Holy Roman Emperor, much to the dismay of Frederick and Prussia. Not only that, Britain would soon join the Austro-Russian alliance, but complications arose. Britain's basic framework for the alliance itself was to protect Hanover's interests against France. At the same time, Kaunitz kept approaching the French in the hope of establishing just such an alliance with Austria. Not only that, France had no intention to ally with Russia, who, years earlier, had meddled in France's affairs during Austria's succession war. France also saw the dismemberment of Prussia as threatening to the stability of Central Europe.</p>
<p>Years later, Kaunitz kept trying to establish France's alliance with Austria. He tried as hard as he could to avoid Austrian entanglement in Hanover's political affairs, and was even willing to trade <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Netherlands" title="Austrian Netherlands">Austrian Netherlands</a> for France's aid in recapturing Silesia. Frustrated by this decision and by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>'s insistence on neutrality, Britain soon turned to Russia. On 30 September 1755, Britain pledged financial aid to Russia in order to station 50,000 troops on the Livonian-Lithuanian border, so they could defend Britain's interests in Hanover immediately. Besthuzev, assuming the preparation was directed against Prussia, was more than happy to obey the request of the British. Unbeknownst to the other powers, King George II also made overtures to the Prussian king, Frederick, who, fearing the Austro-Russian intentions, was also desirous of a rapprochement with Britain. On 16 January 1756, the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Westminster" class="mw-redirect" title="Convention of Westminster">Convention of Westminster</a> was signed, whereby Britain and Prussia promised to aid one another; the parties hoped to achieve lasting peace and stability in Europe.</p>
<p>The carefully coded word in the agreement proved no less catalytic for the other European powers. The results were absolute chaos. Empress Elizabeth of Russia was outraged at the duplicity of Britain's position. Not only that, but France was enraged, and terrified, by the sudden betrayal of its only ally. Austria, particularly Kaunitz, used this situation to their utmost advantage. Now-isolated France was forced to accede to the Austro-Russian alliance or face ruin. Thereafter, on 1 May 1756, the <a href="/wiki/First_Treaty_of_Versailles" class="mw-redirect" title="First Treaty of Versailles">First Treaty of Versailles</a> was signed, in which both nations pledged 24,000 troops to defend each other in the case of an attack. This diplomatic revolution proved to be an important cause of the war; although both treaties were self-defensive in nature, the actions of both coalitions made the war virtually inevitable.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_North_America">In North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: In North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg/300px-Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg.png" width="300" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg/450px-Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg/600px-Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1530" data-file-height="1090" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the British and French settlements in North America in 1750, before the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> (1754 to 1763), that was part of the Seven Years' War</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The boundary between British and French possessions in North America was largely undefined in the 1750s. France had long claimed the entire <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> basin. This was disputed by Britain. In the early 1750s the French began constructing a chain of forts in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio River Valley">Ohio River Valley</a> to assert their claim and shield the Native American population from increasing British influence.</p>
<p>The British settlers along the coast were upset that French troops would now be close to the western borders of their colonies. They felt the French would encourage their tribal allies among the North American natives to attack them. Also, the British settlers wanted access to the fertile land of the Ohio River Valley for the new settlers that were flooding into the British colonies seeking farm land.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderson.2C_p._17_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson.2C_p._17-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most important French fort planned was intended to occupy a position at "the Forks" where the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela Rivers</a> meet to form the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> (present day <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania). Peaceful British attempts to halt this fort construction were unsuccessful, and the French proceeded to build the fort they named <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne" title="Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a>. British colonial militia from Virginia were then sent to drive them out. Led by <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>, they ambushed a small French force at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen" title="Battle of Jumonville Glen">Jumonville Glen</a> on 28 May 1754 killing ten, including commander <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Coulon_de_Jumonville" title="Joseph Coulon de Jumonville">Jumonville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The French retaliated by attacking Washington's army at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Necessity" title="Battle of Fort Necessity">Fort Necessity</a> on 3 July 1754 and forced Washington to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-AndersonCrucible51_9_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndersonCrucible51_9-10">[10]</a></sup> These were the first engagements of what would become the worldwide Seven Years' War.</p>
<p>News of this arrived in Europe, where Britain and France unsuccessfully attempted to negotiate a solution. The two nations eventually dispatched regular troops to North America to enforce their claims. The first British action was the assault on <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a> on 16 June 1755 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Beaus%C3%A9jour" title="Battle of Fort Beauséjour">Battle of Fort Beauséjour</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> which was immediately followed by their <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">expulsion of the Acadians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In July British Major General <a href="/wiki/Edward_Braddock" title="Edward Braddock">Edward Braddock</a> led about 2,000 army troops and provincial militia on an expedition to retake Fort Duquesne, but <a href="/wiki/Braddock_Expedition" title="Braddock Expedition">the expedition</a> ended in disastrous defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In further action, Admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Boscawen" title="Edward Boscawen">Edward Boscawen</a> fired on the French ship <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Alcide_(1742)" title="French ship Alcide (1742)">Alcide</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Action_of_8_June_1755" title="Action of 8 June 1755">on 8 June 1755</a>, capturing it and two troop ships. In September 1755, British colonial and French troops met in the inconclusive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_George" title="Battle of Lake George">Battle of Lake George</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British also harassed French shipping beginning in August 1755, seizing hundreds of ships and capturing thousands of merchant seamen while the two nations were nominally at peace. Incensed, France prepared to attack Hanover, whose <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">prince-elector</a> was also the King of Great Britain and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>. Britain concluded a treaty whereby Prussia agreed to protect Hanover. In response France concluded an alliance with its long-time enemy Austria, an event known as the <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">Diplomatic Revolution</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategies">Strategies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Strategies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For much of the eighteenth century, France approached its wars in the same way. It would let colonies defend themselves or would offer only minimal help (sending them limited numbers of troops or inexperienced soldiers), anticipating that fights for the colonies would most likely be lost anyway.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> This strategy was to a degree forced upon France: geography, coupled with the superiority of the British navy, made it difficult for the French navy to provide significant supplies and support to overseas colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Similarly, several long land borders made an effective domestic army imperative for any French ruler.<sup id="cite_ref-borneman_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borneman-17">[17]</a></sup> Given these military necessities, the French government, unsurprisingly, based its strategy overwhelmingly on the army in Europe: it would keep most of its army on the continent, hoping for victories closer to home.<sup id="cite_ref-borneman_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borneman-17">[17]</a></sup> The plan was to fight to the end of hostilities and then, in treaty negotiations, to trade territorial acquisitions in Europe to regain lost overseas possessions (as had happened in, <i>e.g.</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint-Germain-en-Laye_(1632)" title="Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1632)">Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1632)</a>). This approach did not serve France well in the war, as the colonies were indeed lost, but although much of the European war went well, by its end France had few counterbalancing European successes.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg/220px-Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg/330px-Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg/440px-Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="745" data-file-height="512" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erstes_pr._Bataillon_Leibgarde_in_Schlacht_bei_Kollin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prussian <a href="/wiki/Leibgarde_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Leibgarde (military)">Leibgarde</a> battalion at Kolin, 1757</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The British—by inclination as well as for practical reasons—had tended to avoid large-scale commitments of troops on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> They sought to offset the disadvantage of this in Europe by allying themselves with one or more continental powers whose interests were antithetical to those of their enemies, particularly France.<sup id="cite_ref-Schweizer_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schweizer-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:15–16</sup> By subsidising the armies of continental allies, Britain could turn London's enormous financial power to <a href="/wiki/Golden_Cavalry_of_St_George" title="Golden Cavalry of St George">military advantage</a>. In the Seven Years' War, the British chose as their principal partner the most brilliant general of the day, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> of Prussia, then the rising power in central Europe, and paid Frederick substantial subsidies for his campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-Schweizer_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schweizer-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:106</sup> This was accomplished in the diplomatic revolution of 1756, in which Britain ended its long-standing alliance with Austria in favor of Prussia, leaving Austria to side with France. In marked contrast to France, Britain strove to prosecute the war actively in the colonies, taking full advantage of its <a href="/wiki/Naval_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval power">naval power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-black_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-black-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Simms_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simms-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:64–66</sup> The British pursued a dual strategy – <a href="/wiki/Naval_blockade" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval blockade">naval blockade</a> and bombardment of enemy ports, and rapid movement of troops by sea.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> They harassed enemy shipping and attacked enemy colonies, frequently using colonists from nearby British colonies in the effort.</p>
<p>The Russians and the Austrians were determined to reduce the power of Prussia; the new threat on their doorstep. Along with France, they agreed in 1756 to mutual defense and an attack by Austria and Russia on Prussia, subsidized by France.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div id="Seven_Years.27_War:British_Amphibious_Descents_.281757-61.29" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a class="mw-selflink selflink"><span class="wrap">Seven Years' War</span></a>:<br />
<a href="/wiki/British_Amphibious_Descents_(1757-61)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Amphibious Descents (1757-61)"><span class="wrap">British Amphibious Descents (1757-61)</span></a></span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">

<li><a href="/wiki/Raid_on_St_Malo" title="Raid on St Malo">St Malo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Cherbourg" title="Raid on Cherbourg">Cherbourg</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saint_Cast" title="Battle of Saint Cast">Saint Cast</a></li>

<p><a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Elder" class="mw-redirect" title="William Pitt the Elder">William Pitt the Elder</a>, who entered the cabinet in 1756, had a grand vision for the war that made it entirely different from previous wars with France. As prime minister, Pitt committed Britain to a grand strategy of seizing the entire French Empire, especially its possessions in North America and India. Britain's main weapon was the Royal Navy, which could control the seas and bring as many invasion troops as were needed. He also planned to use colonial forces from the thirteen American colonies, working under the command of British <a href="/wiki/Regular_army" title="Regular army">regulars</a>, to invade New France. In order to tie the French army down he subsidized his European allies. Pitt was head of the government from 1756 to 1761, and even after that the British continued his strategy. It proved completely successful.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Pitt had a clear appreciation of the enormous value of imperial possessions, and realized the vulnerability of the French Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1756">1756</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1756">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" width="38" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:
<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Admiral_John_Byng%27s_account_of_the_Battle_of_Minorca_(1756)" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Admiral John Byng's account of the Battle of Minorca (1756)">Admiral John Byng's account of the Battle of Minorca (1756)</a></b></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The British prime minister, the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pelham-Holles,_1st_Duke_of_Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Pelham-Holles, 1st Duke of Newcastle-upon-Tyne">Duke of Newcastle</a>, was optimistic that the new series of alliances could prevent war from breaking out in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> However, a large French force was assembled at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>, and the French opened the campaign against the British by an <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Menorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Menorca">attack on Menorca</a> in the Mediterranean. A British attempt at relief was foiled at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Minorca_(1756)" title="Battle of Minorca (1756)">Battle of Minorca</a>, and the island was captured on 28 June (for which <a href="/wiki/John_Byng" title="John Byng">Admiral Byng</a> was court-martialed and executed).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Britain formally declared war on France on 17 May,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> nearly two years after fighting had broken out in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Country" title="Ohio Country">Ohio Country</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lobositz.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Battle_of_Lobositz.png/300px-Battle_of_Lobositz.png" width="300" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Battle_of_Lobositz.png/450px-Battle_of_Lobositz.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Battle_of_Lobositz.png/600px-Battle_of_Lobositz.png 2x" data-file-width="1089" data-file-height="636" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lobositz.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lobositz" title="Battle of Lobositz">Battle of Lobositz</a>. Austria: blue; Prussia: red.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Frederick&#160;II of Prussia had received reports of the clashes in North America and had <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Prussian_alliance_(1756)" title="Anglo-Prussian alliance (1756)">formed an alliance with Great Britain</a>. On 29 August 1756, he led Prussian troops across the border of Saxony, one of the small German states in league with Austria. He intended this as a bold pre-emption of an anticipated Austro-French invasion of Silesia. He had three goals in his new war on Austria. First, he would seize Saxony and eliminate it as a threat to Prussia, then use the Saxon army and treasury to aid the Prussian war effort. His second goal was to advance into Bohemia, where he might set up winter quarters at Austria's expense. Thirdly, he wanted to invade <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> from Silesia, seize the fortress at Olmütz, and advance on Vienna to force an end to the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._427._30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._427.-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Accordingly, leaving Field Marshal Count <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Christoph_Graf_von_Schwerin" title="Kurt Christoph Graf von Schwerin">Kurt von Schwerin</a> in Silesia with 25,000 soldiers to guard against incursions from Moravia and Hungary, and leaving Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Hans_von_Lehwaldt" title="Hans von Lehwaldt">Hans von Lehwaldt</a> in East Prussia to guard against Russian invasion from the east, Frederick set off with his army for Saxony. The Prussian army marched in three columns. On the right was a column of about 15,000 men under the command of <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ferdinand_of_Brunswick-Wolfenb%C3%BCttel" title="Duke Ferdinand of Brunswick-Wolfenbüttel">Prince Ferdinand of Brunswick</a>. On the left was a column of 18,000 men under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Augustus_William,_Duke_of_Brunswick-Bevern" title="Augustus William, Duke of Brunswick-Bevern">Duke of Brunswick-Bevern</a>. In the centre was Frederick II, himself with Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/James_Francis_Edward_Keith" title="James Francis Edward Keith">James Keith</a> commanding a corps of 30,000 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._427._30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._427.-30">[30]</a></sup> Ferdinand of Brunswick was to close in on the town of <a href="/wiki/Chemnitz" title="Chemnitz">Chemnitz</a>. The Duke of Brunswick-Bevern was to traverse <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a> to close in on <a href="/wiki/Bautzen" title="Bautzen">Bautzen</a>. Meanwhile, Frederick and Keith would make for <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>.</p>
<p>The Saxon and Austrian armies were unprepared, and their forces were scattered. Frederick occupied Dresden with little or no opposition from the Saxons.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lobositz" title="Battle of Lobositz">Battle of Lobositz</a> on 1 October 1756, Frederick prevented the isolated Saxon army from being reinforced by an Austrian army under General <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Ulysses_Browne" title="Maximilian Ulysses Browne">Browne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The Prussians then occupied Saxony; after the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pirna" title="Siege of Pirna">Siege of Pirna</a>, the Saxon army surrendered in October 1756, and was forcibly incorporated into the Prussian army. The attack on neutral Saxony caused outrage across Europe and led to the strengthening of the anti-Prussian coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The only significant Austrian success was the partial occupation of Silesia. Far from being easy, Frederick's early successes proved indecisive and very costly for Prussia's smaller army. This led him to remark that he did not fight the same Austrians as he had during the previous war.<sup id="cite_ref-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Britain had been surprised by the sudden Prussian offensive but now began shipping supplies and ₤670,000 (equivalent to ₤89.9 million in 2016) to its new ally.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Hanoverian_Army_of_Observation" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanoverian Army of Observation">combined force of allied German states</a> was organised by the British to protect <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a> from French invasion, under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cumberland" title="Prince William, Duke of Cumberland">Duke of Cumberland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The British attempted to persuade the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> to join the alliance, but the request was rejected, as the Dutch wished to remain fully neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Despite the huge disparity in numbers, the year had been successful for the Prussian-led forces on the continent, in contrast to the British campaigns in North America.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1757">1757</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1757">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/220px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/330px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg/440px-Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="377" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht-Kolin-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Kolin">Battle of Kolin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pomeranian_War" title="Pomeranian War">Pomeranian War</a></div>
<p>On 18 April 1757, Frederick II again took the initiative by marching into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">Kingdom of Bohemia</a>, hoping to inflict a decisive defeat on Austrian forces.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> After winning the bloody <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prague_(1757)" title="Battle of Prague (1757)">Battle of Prague</a> on 6 May 1757, in which both forces suffered major casualties, the Prussians forced the Austrians back into the fortifications of Prague. The Prussian army then <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Prague_(1757)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Prague (1757)">laid siege to the city</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In response, Austrian commander <a href="/wiki/Count_Leopold_Joseph_von_Daun" title="Count Leopold Joseph von Daun">Leopold von Daun</a> collected a force of 30,000 men to come to the relief of Prague.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Following the battle at Prague, Frederick took 5,000 troops from the siege at Prague and sent them to reinforce the 19,000-man army under the Duke of Brunswick-Bevern at Kolin in Bohemia.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Von Daun arrived too late to participate in the battle of Prague, but picked up 16,000 men who had escaped from the battle. With this army he slowly moved to relieve Prague. The Prussian army was too weak to simultaneously besiege Prague and keep von Daun away, and Frederick was forced to attack prepared positions. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kolin" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Kolin">Battle of Kolin</a> was a sharp defeat for Frederick, his first. His losses further forced him to lift the siege and withdraw from Bohemia altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg/220px-Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg/330px-Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg/440px-Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2208" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlacht_bei_Ro%C3%9Fbach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rossbach" title="Battle of Rossbach">Battle of Rossbach</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Later that summer, the Russians under Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Fyodorovich_Apraksin" title="Stepan Fyodorovich Apraksin">Stepan Fyodorovich Apraksin</a> besieged <a href="/wiki/Klaip%C4%97da" title="Klaipėda">Memel</a> with 75,000 troops. Memel had one of the strongest fortresses in Prussia. However, after five days of artillery bombardment the Russian army was able to storm it.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._460_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._460-43">[43]</a></sup> The Russians then used Memel as a base to invade <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a> and defeated a smaller Prussian force in the fiercely contested <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gross-J%C3%A4gersdorf" title="Battle of Gross-Jägersdorf">Battle of Gross-Jägersdorf</a> on 30 August 1757. In the words of the American historian Daniel Marston, Gross-Jägersdorf left the Prussians with "a newfound respect for the fighting capabilities of the Russians that was reinforced in the later battles of Zorndorf and Kunersdorf".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> However, the Russians were not yet able to take Königsberg after using up their supplies of cannonballs at Memel and Gross-Jägersdorf and retreated soon afterward. A recurring problem for the Russians throughout the war was their logistics.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22-45">[45]</a></sup> The Russians lacked a quartermaster's department capable of keeping armies operating in Central Europe properly supplied over the primitive mud roads of eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22-45">[45]</a></sup> The tendency of Russian armies to break off operations after fighting a major battle, even when they were not defeated, was less about their casualties and more about their supply lines; after expending much of their munitions in a battle, Russian generals did not wish to risk another battle knowing resupply would be a long time coming.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22-45">[45]</a></sup> This long-standing weakness was evident in the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Russian%E2%80%93Turkish_War_(1735%E2%80%9339)" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Russian–Turkish War (1735–39)">Russian-Ottoman War</a> of 1735–1739, where Russian battle victories led to only modest war gains due to problems supplying their armies.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone.2C_David_page_70_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone.2C_David_page_70-46">[46]</a></sup> The Russian quartermasters department had not improved, so the same problems reoccurred in Prussia.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone.2C_David_page_70_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone.2C_David_page_70-46">[46]</a></sup> Still, the Imperial Russian Army was a new threat to Prussia. Not only was Frederick forced to break off his invasion of Bohemia, he was now forced to withdraw further into Prussian-controlled territory.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> His defeats on the battlefield brought still more opportunistic nations into the war. Sweden declared war on Prussia and invaded Pomerania with 17,000 men.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._460_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._460-43">[43]</a></sup> Sweden felt this small army was all that was needed to occupy Pomerania and felt the Swedish army would not need to engage with the Prussians because the Prussians were occupied on so many other fronts.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg/220px-Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg/330px-Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg/440px-Batte_of_Leuthen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="440" /></a>
