</div>
</div>
<p>Things were looking grim for Prussia now, with the Austrians mobilising to attack Prussian-controlled soil and a combined French and <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsarmee" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichsarmee">Reichsarmee</a></i> (German states) army under <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Rohan,_prince_de_Soubise" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles de Rohan, prince de Soubise">Prince Soubise</a> approaching from the west. The <i>Reichsarmee</i> was a collection of armies from the smaller German states that banded together to heed the appeal of the Holy Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor">Franz I</a> against Frederick.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41-48">[48]</a></sup> However, in November and December 1757, the whole situation in Germany was reversed. First, Frederick devastated Soubise's forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rossbach" title="Battle of Rossbach">Battle of Rossbach</a> on 5 November 1757<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and then routed a vastly superior Austrian force at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leuthen" title="Battle of Leuthen">Battle of Leuthen</a> on 5 December 1757.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Rossbach was the only battle between the French and the Prussians during the entire war.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41-48">[48]</a></sup> At Rossbach, the Prussians lost about 548 men killed while the Franco-German force under Soubise lost about 10,000 killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_42_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_42-51">[51]</a></sup> Frederick always called Leuthen his greatest victory, an assessment shared by many at the time as the Austrian Army was considered to be a highly professional force.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_42_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_42-51">[51]</a></sup> With these victories, Frederick once again established himself as Europe's premier general and his men as Europe's most accomplished soldiers. However, Frederick missed an opportunity to completely destroy the Austrian army at Leuthen and it escaped back into Bohemia. He hoped the two smashing victories would bring Maria Theresa to the peace table, but she was determined not to negotiate until she had re-taken Silesia. Maria Theresia also improved the Austrians' command after Leuthen by replacing her incompetent brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles_Alexander_of_Lorraine" title="Prince Charles Alexander of Lorraine">Charles of Lorraine</a>, with von Daun, who was now a field marshal.</p>
<p>This problem was compounded when the main Hanoverian army under Cumberland was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hastenbeck" title="Battle of Hastenbeck">Battle of Hastenbeck</a> and forced to surrender entirely at the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Klosterzeven" title="Convention of Klosterzeven">Convention of Klosterzeven</a> following a <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Hanover_(1757)" title="Invasion of Hanover (1757)">French Invasion of Hanover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The convention removed Hanover from the war, leaving the western approach to Prussian territory extremely vulnerable. Frederick sent urgent requests to Britain for more substantial assistance, as he was now without any outside military support for his forces in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg/220px-Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg/330px-Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg/440px-Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1650" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bataille_des_Cardinaux_en_1759_peinte_par_Richard_Paton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quiberon_Bay" title="Battle of Quiberon Bay">Battle of Quiberon Bay</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Calculating that no further Russian advance was likely until 1758, Frederick moved the bulk of his eastern forces to Pomerania under the command of Marshal Lehwaldt, where they were to repel the Swedish invasion. In short order, the Prussian army drove the Swedes back, occupied most of <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Pomerania" title="Swedish Pomerania">Swedish Pomerania</a>, and blockaded its capital <a href="/wiki/Stralsund" title="Stralsund">Stralsund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George&#160;II of Great Britain</a>, on the advice of his British ministers after the battle of Rossbach, revoked the Convention of Klosterzeven, and Hanover reentered the war.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Over the winter the new commander of the Hanoverian forces, <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ferdinand_of_Brunswick" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke Ferdinand of Brunswick">Duke Ferdinand of Brunswick</a>, regrouped his army and launched a series of offensives that drove the French back across the <a href="/wiki/River_Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="River Rhine">River Rhine</a>. Ferdinand's forces kept Prussia's western flank secure for the rest of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The British had suffered further defeats in North America, particularly at <a href="/wiki/Fort_William_Henry" title="Fort William Henry">Fort William Henry</a>. At home, however, stability had been established. Since 1756, successive governments led by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pelham-Holles" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Pelham-Holles">Newcastle</a> and Pitt had fallen. In August 1757, the two men agreed to a political partnership and formed a <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a> that gave new, firmer direction to the war effort. The new strategy emphasised both Newcastle's commitment to British involvement on the continent, particularly in defence of Germany, and Pitt's determination to use naval power to seize <a href="/wiki/French_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="French colonies">French colonies</a> around the globe. This "dual strategy" would dominate British policy for the next five years.</p>
<p>Between 10 and 17 October 1757, a Hungarian general, Count <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A1s_Hadik" title="András Hadik">András Hadik</a>, serving in the Austrian army, executed what may be the most famous <a href="/wiki/Hussar" title="Hussar">hussar</a> action in history. When the Prussian king, Frederick, was marching south with his powerful armies, the Hungarian general unexpectedly swung his force of 5,000, mostly hussars, around the Prussians and occupied part of their capital, Berlin, for one night.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._467._57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._467.-57">[57]</a></sup> The city was spared for a negotiated ransom of 200,000 thalers.<sup id="cite_ref-Asprey.2C_p._467._57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asprey.2C_p._467.-57">[57]</a></sup> When Frederick heard about this humiliating occupation, he immediately sent a larger force to free the city. Hadik, however, left the city with his hussars and safely reached the Austrian lines. Subsequently, Hadik was promoted to the rank of marshal in the Austrian Army.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1758">1758</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1758">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 1758, Frederick launched an invasion of <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, and laid siege to <a href="/wiki/Olm%C3%BCtz" class="mw-redirect" title="Olmütz">Olmütz</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Olomouc" title="Olomouc">Olomouc</a>, Czech Republic).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Following an Austrian victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Domstadtl" title="Battle of Domstadtl">Battle of Domstadtl</a> that wiped out a supply convoy destined for Olmütz, Frederick broke off the siege and withdrew from Moravia. It marked the end of his final attempt to launch a major invasion of Austrian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In January 1758, the Russians invaded <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a>, where the province, almost denuded of troops, put up little opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_41-48">[48]</a></sup> East Prussia had been occupied by Russian forces over the winter and would remain under their control until 1762, although it was far less strategically valuable to Prussia than Brandenburg or Silesia. In any case, Frederick did not see the Russians as an immediate threat and instead entertained hopes of first fighting a decisive battle against Austria that would knock them out of the war.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg" width="220" height="351" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="989" data-file-height="1577" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Krefeld_-_Map_of_the_area_printed_in_The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Battle of Krefeld – a map of the area in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gentleman%27s_Magazine" title="The Gentleman's Magazine">The Gentleman's Magazine</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In April 1758, the British concluded the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Prussian_Convention" title="Anglo-Prussian Convention">Anglo-Prussian Convention</a> with Frederick in which they committed to pay him <a href="/wiki/Golden_Cavalry_of_St_George" title="Golden Cavalry of St George">an annual subsidy</a> of £670,000. Britain also dispatched 9,000 troops to reinforce Ferdinand's Hanoverian army, the first British troop commitment on the continent and a reversal in the policy of Pitt. Ferdinand had succeeded in driving the French from Hanover and Westphalia and re-captured the port of <a href="/wiki/Emden" title="Emden">Emden</a> in March 1758 before crossing the Rhine with his own forces, which caused alarm in France. Despite Ferdinand's victory over the French at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krefeld" title="Battle of Krefeld">Battle of Krefeld</a> and the brief occupation of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>, he was compelled by the successful manoeuvering of larger French forces to withdraw across the Rhine.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>By this point Frederick was increasingly concerned by the Russian advance from the east and marched to counter it. Just east of the Oder in Brandenburg-<a href="/wiki/Neumark" title="Neumark">Neumark</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zorndorf" title="Battle of Zorndorf">Battle of Zorndorf</a> (now Sarbinowo, Poland), a Prussian army of 35,000 men under Frederick on 25 August 1758, fought a Russian army of 43,000 commanded by Count <a href="/wiki/William_Fermor" title="William Fermor">William Fermor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Both sides suffered heavy casualties – the Prussians 12,800, the Russians 18,000 – but the Russians withdrew, and Frederick claimed victory.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The American historian Daniel Marston described Zorndorf as a "draw" as both sides were too exhausted and had taken such losses that neither wished to fight another battle with the other.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In the undecided <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tornow" title="Battle of Tornow">Battle of Tornow</a> on 25 September, a Swedish army repulsed six assaults by a Prussian army but did not push on Berlin following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fehrbellin_(1758)" title="Battle of Fehrbellin (1758)">Battle of Fehrbellin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg/220px-La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg/330px-La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg/440px-La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="574" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Pegna_%C3%9Cberfall_bei_Hochkirch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hochkirch" title="Battle of Hochkirch">Battle of Hochkirch</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The war was continuing indecisively when on 14 October Marshal Daun's Austrians surprised the main Prussian army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hochkirch" title="Battle of Hochkirch">Battle of Hochkirch</a> in Saxony.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Frederick lost much of his artillery but retreated in good order, helped by dense woods. The Austrians had ultimately made little progress in the campaign in Saxony despite Hochkirch and had failed to achieve a decisive breakthrough. After a thwarted attempt to take Dresden, Daun's troops were forced to withdraw to Austrian territory for the winter, so that Saxony remained under Prussian occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> At the same time, the Russians failed in an attempt to take <a href="/wiki/Kolberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Kolberg">Kolberg</a> in Pomerania (now <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%82obrzeg" title="Kołobrzeg">Kołobrzeg</a>, Poland) from the Prussians.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In France, 1758 had been disappointing, and in the wake of this a new chief minister, the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Fran%C3%A7ois,_duc_de_Choiseul" title="Étienne François, duc de Choiseul">Duc de Choiseul</a>, was appointed. Choiseul planned to end the war in 1759 by making strong attacks on Britain and Hanover.</p>
<h3><span id="1759–60"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1759.E2.80.9360">1759–60</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1759–60">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year 1759 saw several Prussian defeats. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kay" title="Battle of Kay">Battle of Kay</a>, or Paltzig, the Russian Count <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Semyonovich_Saltykov" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyotr Semyonovich Saltykov">Saltykov</a> with 47,000 Russians defeated 26,000 Prussians commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Carl_Heinrich_von_Wedel" title="Carl Heinrich von Wedel">Carl Heinrich von Wedel</a>. Though the Hanoverians defeated an army of 60,000 French at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Minden" title="Battle of Minden">Minden</a>, Austrian general <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Josef_Graf_Daun" class="mw-redirect" title="Leopold Josef Graf Daun">Daun</a> forced the surrender of an entire Prussian corps of 13,000 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Maxen" title="Battle of Maxen">Battle of Maxen</a>. Frederick himself lost half his army in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kunersdorf" title="Battle of Kunersdorf">Battle of Kunersdorf</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Kunowice" title="Kunowice">Kunowice</a> Poland), the worst defeat in his military career and one that drove him to the brink of abdication and thoughts of suicide. The disaster resulted partly from his misjudgment of the Russians, who had already demonstrated their strength at Zorndorf and at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gross-J%C3%A4gersdorf" title="Battle of Gross-Jägersdorf">Gross-Jägersdorf</a> (now Motornoye, Russia), and partly from good cooperation between the Russian and Austrian forces.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg/220px-HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg/330px-HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg/440px-HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1154" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HGM_Findenigg_Gefecht_bei_Maxen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Maxen" title="Battle of Maxen">Battle of Maxen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The French <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_invasion_of_Britain_(1759)" title="Planned French invasion of Britain (1759)">planned to invade the British Isles</a> during 1759 by accumulating troops near the mouth of the Loire and concentrating their Brest and Toulon fleets. However, two sea defeats prevented this. In August, the Mediterranean fleet under <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_La_Clue-Sabran" title="Jean-François de La Clue-Sabran">Jean-François de La Clue-Sabran</a> was scattered by a larger British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Edward_Boscawen" title="Edward Boscawen">Edward Boscawen</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lagos_(1759)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Lagos (1759)">Battle of Lagos</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quiberon_Bay" title="Battle of Quiberon Bay">Battle of Quiberon Bay</a> on 20 November, the British admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hawke" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Hawke">Edward Hawke</a> with 23 <a href="/wiki/Ship_of_the_line" title="Ship of the line">ships of the line</a> caught the French Brest fleet with 21 ships of the line under <a href="/wiki/Marshal_de_Conflans" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshal de Conflans">Marshal de Conflans</a> and sank, captured, or forced many of them aground, putting an end to the French plans.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg/220px-Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg/330px-Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg/440px-Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="958" data-file-height="580" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Menzel_-_Battle_of_Liegnitz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Liegnitz_(1760)" title="Battle of Liegnitz (1760)">Battle of Liegnitz (1760)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kunersdorff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kunersdorff.jpg/220px-Kunersdorff.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kunersdorff.jpg/330px-Kunersdorff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kunersdorff.jpg/440px-Kunersdorff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kunersdorff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kunersdorf" title="Battle of Kunersdorf">Battle of Kunersdorf</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The year 1760 brought yet more Prussian disasters. The general <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_August,_Baron_de_la_Motte_Fouqu%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich August, Baron de la Motte Fouqué">Fouqué</a> was defeated by the Austrians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Landshut_(1760)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Landshut (1760)">Battle of Landshut</a>. The French captured <a href="/wiki/Marburg" title="Marburg">Marburg</a>, and the Swedes part of <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>. The Hanoverians were victorious over the French at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Warburg" title="Battle of Warburg">Battle of Warburg</a>, their continued success preventing France from sending troops to aid the Austrians against Prussia in the east.</p>
<p>Despite this, the Austrians, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Baron_Ernst_Gideon_von_Laudon" class="mw-redirect" title="Baron Ernst Gideon von Laudon">General Laudon</a>, captured <a href="/wiki/K%C5%82odzko" title="Kłodzko">Glatz</a> (now <a href="/wiki/K%C5%82odzko" title="Kłodzko">Kłodzko</a>, Poland) in Silesia. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Liegnitz_(1760)" title="Battle of Liegnitz (1760)">Battle of Liegnitz</a> Frederick scored a strong victory despite being outnumbered three to one. The Russians under <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Saltykov" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyotr Saltykov">General Saltykov</a> and Austrians under <a href="/wiki/Franz_Moritz_Graf_von_Lacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Franz Moritz Graf von Lacy">General Lacy</a> briefly occupied his capital, Berlin, in October, but could not hold it for long. Still, the loss of Berlin to the Russians and Austrians was a great blow to Frederick's prestige as many pointed out that the Prussians had no hope of occupying temporarily or otherwise St. Petersburg or Vienna. The end of that year saw Frederick once more victorious, defeating the able Daun in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Torgau" title="Battle of Torgau">Battle of Torgau</a>; but he suffered very heavy casualties, and the Austrians retreated in good order.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, after the battle of Kunersdorf, the Russian army was mostly inactive due mostly to their tenuous supply lines.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Russian logistics were so poor that in October 1759, an agreement was signed under which the Austrians undertook to supply the Russians as the quartermaster's department of the Russian Army was badly strained by the demands of Russian armies operating so far from home.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22-45">[45]</a></sup> As it was, the requirement that the Austrian quartermaster's department supply both the Austrian and Russian armies proved beyond its capacity, and in practice, the Russians received little in the way of supplies from the Austrians.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_22-45">[45]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Liegnitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Liegnitz">Liegnitz</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Legnica" title="Legnica">Legnica</a>, Poland), the Russians arrived too late to participate in the battle. They made two attempts to storm the fortress of Kolberg, but neither succeeded. The tenacious resistance of Kolberg allowed Frederick to focus on the Austrians instead of having to split his forces.</p>
<h3><span id="1761–62"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1761.E2.80.9362">1761–62</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1761–62">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg/220px-Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg/330px-Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg/440px-Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1385" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fall_of_Kolberg_in_1761.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kolberg_(1761)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Kolberg (1761)">Siege of Kolberg (1761)</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_invasion_of_Portugal_(1762)" title="Spanish invasion of Portugal (1762)">Spanish invasion of Portugal (1762)</a></div>
<p>Prussia began the 1761 campaign with just 100,000 available troops, many of them new recruits, and its situation seemed desperate.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> However, the Austrian and Russian forces were also heavily depleted and could not launch a major offensive.</p>
<p>In February 1761 <a href="/wiki/Duke_Ferdinand_of_Brunswick" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke Ferdinand of Brunswick">Duke Ferdinand of Brunswick</a> surprised French troops at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Langensalza_(1761)" title="Battle of Langensalza (1761)">Langensalza</a> and then advanced to <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Cassel_(1761)" title="Siege of Cassel (1761)">besiege Cassel</a> in March. He was forced to lift the siege and retreat after French forces regrouped and captured several thousand of his men at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gr%C3%BCnberg" title="Battle of Grünberg">Battle of Grünberg</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Villinghausen" title="Battle of Villinghausen">Battle of Villinghausen</a>, forces under Prince <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_of_Brunswick" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand of Brunswick">Ferdinand of Brunswick</a> defeated a 92,000-man French army.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:7yearswar.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/7yearswar.PNG/235px-7yearswar.PNG" width="235" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/7yearswar.PNG/353px-7yearswar.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/7yearswar.PNG/470px-7yearswar.PNG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1568" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:7yearswar.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Operations of Russian army on Polish-Lithuanian territory, 1756–1763</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the eastern front, progress was very slow. The Russian army was heavily dependent upon its main magazines in Poland, and the Prussian army launched several successful raids against them. One of them, led by general Platen in September resulted in the loss of 2,000 Russians, mostly captured, and the destruction of 5,000 wagons.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-70">[70]</a></sup> Deprived of men, the Prussians had to resort to this new sort of warfare, raiding, to delay the advance of their enemies. Nonetheless, at the end of the year, they suffered two critical setbacks. The Russians under <a href="/wiki/Zakhar_Chernyshev" class="mw-redirect" title="Zakhar Chernyshev">Zakhar Chernyshev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Rumyantsev" title="Pyotr Rumyantsev">Pyotr Rumyantsev</a> <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kolberg_(1761)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Kolberg (1761)">stormed Kolberg in Pomerania</a>, while the Austrians captured <a href="/wiki/Schweidnitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Schweidnitz">Schweidnitz</a>. The loss of Kolberg cost Prussia its last port on the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> A major problem for the Russians throughout the war had always been their weak logistics, which prevented their generals from following up their victories, and now with the fall of Kolberg, the Russians could at long last supply their armies in Central Europe via the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone.2C_David_page_75_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone.2C_David_page_75-72">[72]</a></sup> The fact that the Russians could now supply their armies over the sea, which was considerably faster and safer (Prussian cavalry could not intercept Russian ships in the Baltic) than over the land threatened to swing the balance of power decisively against Prussia.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone.2C_David_page_75_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone.2C_David_page_75-72">[72]</a></sup> In Britain, it was speculated that a total Prussian collapse was now imminent.</p>
<p>Britain now threatened to withdraw its subsidies if Prussia did not consider offering concessions to secure peace. As the Prussian armies had dwindled to just 60,000 men and with Berlin itself about to come under siege, Frederick's survival was severely threatened. Then on 5 January 1762 the Russian <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia" title="Elizabeth of Russia">Empress Elizabeth</a> died. Her Prussophile successor, <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">Peter III</a>, at once ended the Russian occupation of East Prussia and Pomerania (see: the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint_Petersburg_(1762)" title="Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1762)">Treaty of Saint Petersburg (1762)</a>) and mediated Frederick's truce with Sweden. He also placed a corps of his own troops under Frederick's command. Frederick was then able to muster a larger army, of 120,000 men, and concentrate it against Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-70">[70]</a></sup> He drove them from much of Silesia, while his brother Henry won a victory in Saxony in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Freiberg" title="Battle of Freiberg">Battle of Freiberg</a> (29 October 1762). At the same time, his Brunswick allies captured the key town of <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ttingen" title="Göttingen">Göttingen</a> and compounded this by <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Cassel" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Cassel">taking Cassel</a>.</p>
<p>1762 brought two new countries into the war. Britain declared war against <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a> on 4 January 1762; Spain reacted by issuing their own declaration of war against Britain on 18 January.<sup id="cite_ref-Fish2003p2_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fish2003p2-73">[73]</a></sup> Portugal followed by joining the war on Britain's side. <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Portugal_(1762)" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Portugal (1762)">Spain, aided by the French, launched an invasion of Portugal</a> and succeeded in <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Almeida_(1762)" title="Siege of Almeida (1762)">capturing Almeida</a>. The arrival of British reinforcements stalled a further Spanish advance, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Valencia_de_Alc%C3%A1ntara" title="Battle of Valencia de Alcántara">Battle of Valencia de Alcántara</a> saw British-Portuguese forces overrun a major Spanish supply base. The invaders were stopped on the heights in front of <a href="/wiki/Abrantes_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Abrantes Municipality">Abrantes</a> (called <i>the pass to Lisbon</i>) where the Anglo-Portuguese were entrenched. Eventually the Anglo-Portuguese army, aided by guerrillas and practicing a <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> strategy,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> chased the greatly reduced Franco-Spanish army back to Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> recovering almost all the lost towns, among them the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Headquarters" title="Headquarters">headquarters</a> in <a href="/wiki/Castelo_Branco,_Portugal" title="Castelo Branco, Portugal">Castelo Branco</a> full of wounded and sick that had been left behind.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the long British naval blockade of French ports had sapped the morale of the French populace. Morale declined further when news of defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Signal_Hill" title="Battle of Signal Hill">Battle of Signal Hill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Colony of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> reached Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1763">1763</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1763">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg/220px-Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg" width="220" height="347" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg/330px-Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg/440px-Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hubertusburg_Allegorie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a></div>
<p>By 1763, the war in central Europe was essentially a stalemate between Prussia and Austria. Prussia had retaken nearly all of Silesia from the Austrians, and after Prussia's 1762 victory at the Battle of Freiberg Frederick held most of Saxony but not its capital, Dresden. His financial situation was not dire, but his kingdom was devastated and his army severely weakened. His manpower had dramatically decreased, and he had lost so many effective officers and generals that an offensive against Dresden seemed impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled-34">[34]</a></sup> British subsidies had been stopped by the new prime minister, <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart,_3rd_Earl_of_Bute" title="John Stuart, 3rd Earl of Bute">Lord Bute</a>, and the Russian emperor had been overthrown by his wife, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine</a>, who ended Russia's alliance with Prussia and withdrew from the war. Austria, however, like most participants, was facing a severe financial crisis and had to decrease the size of its army, something which greatly affected its offensive power.<sup id="cite_ref-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frederick_II.2C_Jean-Paul_Bled-34">[34]</a></sup> Indeed, after having effectively sustained a long war, its administration was in disarray.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> By that time, it still held Dresden, the southeastern parts of Saxony, and the county of Glatz in southern Silesia, but the prospect of victory was dim without Russian support and Maria Theresa had largely given up her hopes of re-conquering Silesia. In 1763 a peace settlement was reached at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a>, in which Glatz was returned to Prussia in exchange for the Prussian evacuation of Saxony. This ended the war in central Europe.</p>
<p>The stalemate had really been reached by 1759–1760; Prussia and Austria were nearly out of money. The materials of both sides had been largely consumed. Frederick was no longer receiving subsidies from Britain; the Golden Cavalry of St. George had produced nearly 13 million dollars (equivalent). He had melted and coined most of the church silver, had ransacked the palaces of his kingdom and coined that silver, and reduced his purchasing power by mixing it with copper. His banks' capital was exhausted, and he had pawned nearly everything of value from his own estate. While Frederick still had a significant amount of money left from the prior British subsidies, he hoped to use it to restore his kingdom's prosperity in peacetime; in any case, Prussia's population was so depleted that he could not sustain another long campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Similarly, Marie Theresa had reached the limit of her resources. She had pawned her jewels in 1758; in 1760, she approved a public subscription for support and urged her public to bring their silver to the mint. French subsidies were no longer provided.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahantheresa_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahantheresa-84">[84]</a></sup> Although she had many young men still to draft, she could not conscript them and did not dare to resort to the impressment Frederick had done.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> She had even dismissed some men because it was too expensive to feed them.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahantheresa_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahantheresa-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="British_amphibious_&quot;descents&quot;"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_amphibious_.22descents.22">British amphibious "descents"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: British amphibious &quot;descents&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Rochefort" title="Raid on Rochefort">Raid on Rochefort</a></div>
<p>Great Britain planned a "descent" (an <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious demonstration</a> or raid) on <a href="/wiki/Rochefort,_Charente-Maritime" title="Rochefort, Charente-Maritime">Rochefort</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Joint_warfare" title="Joint warfare">joint operation</a> to overrun the town and burn shipping in the <a href="/wiki/Charente_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Charente river">Charente</a>. The expedition set out on 8 September 1757, <a href="/wiki/John_Mordaunt_(general)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Mordaunt (general)">Sir John Mordaunt</a> commanding the troops and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hawke" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Hawke">Sir Edward Hawke</a> the fleet. On 23 September the <a href="/wiki/Isle_d%27Aix" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle d'Aix">Isle d'Aix</a> was taken, but military staff dithered and lost so much time that Rochefort became unassailable.<sup id="cite_ref-Combined1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Combined1-86">[86]</a></sup> The expedition abandoned the Isle d'Aix, returning to Great Britain on 1 October.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Pitt,_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg/220px-William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg" width="220" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg/330px-William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg/440px-William_Pitt%2C_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3051" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Pitt,_1st_Earl_of_Chatham_by_William_Hoare.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Under Pitt's leadership, Britain's position as the leading colonial power was confirmed by the Seven Years' War.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite the debatable strategic success and the operational failure of the descent on Rochefort, William Pitt—who saw purpose in this type of asymmetric enterprise—prepared to continue such operations.<sup id="cite_ref-Combined1_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Combined1-86">[86]</a></sup> An army was assembled under the command of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Spencer,_3rd_Duke_of_Marlborough" title="Charles Spencer, 3rd Duke of Marlborough">Charles Spencer, 3rd Duke of Marlborough</a>; he was aided by <a href="/wiki/George_Germain,_1st_Viscount_Sackville" title="George Germain, 1st Viscount Sackville">Lord George Sackville</a>. The naval squadron and transports for the expedition were commanded by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Howe,_1st_Earl_Howe" title="Richard Howe, 1st Earl Howe">Richard Howe</a>. The army landed on 5 June 1758 at <a href="/wiki/Cancalle_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Cancalle Bay">Cancalle Bay</a>, proceeded to <a href="/wiki/St._Malo" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Malo">St.&#160;Malo</a>, and, finding that it would take prolonged siege to capture it, instead attacked the nearby port of St.&#160;Servan. It burned shipping in the harbor, roughly 80 French privateers and merchantmen, as well as four warships which were under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The force then re-embarked under threat of the arrival of French relief forces. An attack on <a href="/wiki/Le_Havre" title="Le Havre">Havre de Grace</a> was called off, and the fleet sailed on to <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg-Octeville" title="Cherbourg-Octeville">Cherbourg</a>; the weather being bad and provisions low, that too was abandoned, and the expedition returned having damaged French privateering and provided further strategic demonstration against the French coast.</p>
<p>Pitt now prepared to send troops into Germany; and both Marlborough and Sackville, disgusted by what they perceived as the futility of the "descents", obtained commissions in that army. The elderly <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bligh" title="Thomas Bligh">General Bligh</a> was appointed to command a new "descent", escorted by Howe. The campaign began propitiously with the <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Cherbourg" title="Raid on Cherbourg">Raid on Cherbourg</a>. Covered by naval bombardment, the army drove off the French force detailed to oppose their landing, captured Cherbourg, and destroyed its fortifications, docks, and shipping.</p>
<p>The troops were reembarked and moved to the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_St._Lunaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of St. Lunaire">Bay of St.&#160;Lunaire</a> in Brittany where, on 3 September, they were landed to operate against St.&#160;Malo; however, this action proved impractical. Worsening weather forced the two armies to separate: the ships sailed for the safer anchorage of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Cast-le-Guildo" title="Saint-Cast-le-Guildo">St.&#160;Cast</a>, while the army proceeded overland. The tardiness of Bligh in moving his forces allowed a French force of 10,000 from <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> to catch up with him and open fire on the reembarkation troops. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saint_Cast" title="Battle of Saint Cast">battle of Saint Cast</a> a rear-guard of 1,400 under Dury held off the French while the rest of the army embarked. They could not be saved; 750, including Dury, were killed and the rest captured.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonies">Colonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Colonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Seven_Years.27_War:West_Indies_Campaign" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">

</div>
<div id="Seven_Years.27_War:West_Indies_Campaign" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a class="mw-selflink selflink"><span class="wrap">Seven Years' War</span></a>:<br />
West Indies Campaign</span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">

<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Windward_Passage" title="Battle of the Windward Passage">Windward Passage</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Dominica" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Dominica">Dominica</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Martinique_(1762)" title="Invasion of Martinique (1762)">2nd Martinique</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Havana_(1762)" title="Battle of Havana (1762)">Havana</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>The colonial conflict mainly between France and Britain took place in India, North America, Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> isles, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and coastal Africa. Over the course of the war, Great Britain gained enormous areas of land and influence at the expense of the French.</p>
<p>Great Britain lost <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a> in the Mediterranean to the French in 1756 but captured the French colonies in <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> in 1758. The British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> took the French sugar colonies of <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Guadeloupe_(1759)" title="Invasion of Guadeloupe (1759)">Guadeloupe</a> in 1759 and <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Martinique" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Martinique">Martinique</a> in 1762 as well as the Spanish cities of <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Cuba" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Cuba">Havana in Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1762)" title="Battle of Manila (1762)">Manila</a> in the Philippines, both prominent Spanish colonial cities. However, expansion into the hinterlands of both cities met with stiff resistance. In the Philippines, the British were <a href="/wiki/British_occupation_of_Manila" title="British occupation of Manila">confined to Manila</a> until their agreed upon withdrawal at the war's end.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a></div>
