<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:307px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/305px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" width="305" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/458px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/610px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1120" data-file-height="853" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
French and British positions during the first four years of the war
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F4A8C8; color:#FF002F; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"><span class="legend-text">■ ◘</span></span>&#160;British territory, forts and settlements</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A8C4F4; color:#425BFC; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"><span class="legend-text">■ ◘</span></span>&#160;French territory, forts and settlements</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the war, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Nations_of_The_Iroquois_Confederacy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Seven Nations of The Iroquois Confederacy (page does not exist)">Seven Nations of The Iroquois Confederacy</a> were allied with the French. These were Native Americans of the Laurentian valley—the <a href="/wiki/Algonquin_people" title="Algonquin people">Algonquin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Abenaki_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abenaki people">Abenaki</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Huron_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Huron people">Huron</a>, and others. Although the Algonquin tribes and the Seven Nations were not directly concerned with the fate of the Ohio River Valley, they had been victims of the Iroquois Confederation which included the Seneca, Mohawk, Oneida, Onondaga, Cayuga and Tuscarora tribes. The Iroquois had encroached on Algonquin territory and pushed the Algonquins west beyond Lake Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Therefore, the Algonquin and the Seven Nations were interested in fighting against the Iroquois. Throughout New England, New York, and the North-west Native American tribes formed differing alliances with the major belligerents. The <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a>, dominant in what is now <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a>, sided with the British but did not play a large role in the war.</p>
<p>In 1756 and 1757 the French captured forts <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Oswego_(1756)" title="Battle of Fort Oswego (1756)">Oswego</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_William_Henry" title="Siege of Fort William Henry">William Henry</a> from the British.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The latter victory was marred when France's native allies broke the terms of capitulation and attacked the retreating British column, which was under French guard, slaughtering and scalping soldiers and taking captive many men, women and children while the French refused to protect their captives.<sup id="cite_ref-Dodge91_2_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dodge91_2-91">[91]</a></sup> French naval deployments in 1757 also <a href="/wiki/Louisbourg_Expedition_(1757)" title="Louisbourg Expedition (1757)">successfully defended</a> the key <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Fortress of Louisbourg</a> on <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> called Ile du Roi by the French, securing the seaward approaches to Quebec.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>British Prime Minister William Pitt's focus on the colonies for the 1758 campaign paid off with the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Louisbourg_(1758)" title="Siege of Louisbourg (1758)">taking of Louisbourg</a> after French reinforcements were blocked by British naval victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_(1758)" title="Battle of Cartagena (1758)">Battle of Cartagena</a> and in the successful <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Expedition" title="Forbes Expedition">capture of Fort Duquesne</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Frontenac" title="Battle of Fort Frontenac">Fort Frontenac</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The British also continued the process of deporting the Acadian population with a wave of major operations against <a href="/wiki/Ile_Saint-Jean_Campaign" title="Ile Saint-Jean Campaign">Île Saint-Jean</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>), the <a href="/wiki/St._John_River_Campaign" title="St. John River Campaign">St.&#160;John River valley</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Petitcodiac_River_Campaign" title="Petitcodiac River Campaign">Petitcodiac River valley</a>. The celebration of these successes was dampened by their embarrassing defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carillon" title="Battle of Carillon">Battle of Carillon</a> (Ticonderoga), in which 4,000 French troops repulsed 16,000 British. When the British led by generals <a href="/wiki/James_Abercrombie_(British_Army_officer,_born_1706)" title="James Abercrombie (British Army officer, born 1706)">James Abercrombie</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Howe,_3rd_Viscount_Howe" title="George Howe, 3rd Viscount Howe">George Howe</a> attacked, they believed that the French led by general <a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_de_Montcalm" title="Louis-Joseph de Montcalm">Marquis de Montcalm</a> were defended only by a small <a href="/wiki/Abatis" title="Abatis">abatis</a> which could be taken easily given the British force's significant numerical advantage. The British offensive which was supposed to advance in tight columns and overwhelm the French defenders fell into confusion and scattered, leaving large spaces in their ranks. When the French <a href="/wiki/Chevalier_de_Levis" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevalier de Levis">Chevalier de Levis</a> sent 1,000 soldiers to reinforce Montcalm's struggling troops, the British were pinned down in the brush by intense French musket fire and they were forced to retreat.</p>
<p>All of Britain's campaigns against New France succeeded in 1759, part of what became known as an <a href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_of_1759" title="Annus Mirabilis of 1759"><i>Annus Mirabilis</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Niagara" title="Battle of Fort Niagara">Fort Niagara</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ticonderoga_(1759)" title="Battle of Ticonderoga (1759)">Fort Carillon</a><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> on 8 July 1758 fell to sizable British forces, cutting off French frontier forts further west. Starting in June 1759, the British under <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">James Wolfe</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Murray_(British_Army_officer,_born_1721)" title="James Murray (British Army officer, born 1721)">James Murray</a> set up camp on the Ile d'Orleans across the St. Lawrence River from Quebec, enabling them to commence the 3-month siege that ensued. The French under the Marquis de Montcalm anticipated a British assault to the east of Quebec so he ordered his soldiers to fortify the region of <a href="/wiki/Beauport,_Quebec_City" title="Beauport, Quebec City">Beauport</a>. On July 31 the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Beauport" title="Battle of Beauport">British attacked</a> with 4,000 soldiers but the French positioned high up on the cliffs overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Montmorency_Falls" title="Montmorency Falls">Montmorency Falls</a> forced the British forces to withdraw to the Ile D'Orleans. While Wolfe and Murray planned a second offensive, British rangers raided French settlements along the St. Lawrence, destroying food supplies, ammunition and other goods in an attempt to vanquish the French through starvation. On 13 September 1759, General James Wolfe led 5,000 troops up a goat path to the <a href="/wiki/Plains_of_Abraham" title="Plains of Abraham">Plains of Abraham</a>, 1 mile west of Quebec City. He had positioned his army between Montcalm's forces an hour's march to the east and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_de_Bougainville" title="Louis Antoine de Bougainville">Bougainville</a>'s regiments to the west, which could be mobilised within 3 hours. Instead of waiting for a coordinated attack with Bougainville, Montcalm attacked immediately. When his 3,500 troops advanced, their lines became scattered in a disorderly formation. Many French soldiers fired before they were within range of striking the British. Wolfe organised his troops in two lines stretching 1 mile across the Plains of Abraham. They were ordered to load their Brown Bess rifles with two bullets to obtain maximum power and hold their fire until the French soldiers came within 40 paces of the British ranks. When Montcalm's army was within range of the British, their volley was powerful and nearly all bullets hit their targets, devastating the French ranks. The French fled the Plains of Abraham in a state of utter confusion while they were pursued by members of the Scottish Fraser regiment and other British forces. Despite being cut down by musket fire from the Canadiens and their indigenous allies, the British vastly outnumbered these opponents and won the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Battle of the Plains of Abraham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> General Wolfe was mortally wounded in the chest early in the battle so the command fell to James Murray, who would become the lieutenant governor of Quebec after the war. The Marquis de Montcalm was also severely wounded later in the battle and died the following day. The French Canadians led by the Chevalier de Levis staged a counteroffensive on the Plains of Abraham in the spring of 1760, with initial success at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sainte-Foy" title="Battle of Sainte-Foy">Battle of Sainte-Foy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> but they were unable to retake Quebec, due to British naval superiority following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neuville" title="Battle of Neuville">Battle of Neuville</a>. The French forces retreated to <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, where on 8 September they surrendered to overwhelming British numerical superiority.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West,1770.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg/220px-The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg/330px-The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg/440px-The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West%2C1770.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Death_of_General_Wolfe_B.West,1770.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe" title="The Death of General Wolfe">The Death of General Wolfe</a></i> (1771), on the Plains of Abraham, near Quebec</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seeing French and Indian defeat, in 1760 the Seven Nations of The Iroquois Confederacy resigned from the war and negotiated the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Treaty_of_Kahnawake&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Treaty of Kahnawake (page does not exist)">Treaty of Kahnawake</a> with the British. Among its conditions was their unrestricted travel between Canada and New York, as the nations had extensive trade between Montreal and Albany as well as populations living throughout the area.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1762, towards the end of the war, French forces attacked <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador">St.&#160;John's, Newfoundland</a>. If successful, the expedition would have strengthened France's hand at the negotiating table. Although they took St. John's and raided nearby settlements, the French forces were eventually defeated by British troops at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Signal_Hill" title="Battle of Signal Hill">Battle of Signal Hill</a>. This was the final battle of the war in North America, and it forced the French to surrender to <a href="/wiki/William_Amherst_(British_Army_officer)" title="William Amherst (British Army officer)">Lieutenant Colonel William Amherst</a>. The victorious British now controlled all of eastern North America.</p>
<p>The history of the Seven Years' War in North America, particularly the expulsion of the Acadians, the siege of Quebec, the death of Wolfe, and the Battle of Fort William Henry generated a vast number of ballads, broadsides, images, and novels (see <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Longfellow</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Evangeline" title="Evangeline">Evangeline</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_West" title="Benjamin West">Benjamin West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Death_of_General_Wolfe" title="The Death of General Wolfe">The Death of General Wolfe</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/James_Fenimore_Cooper" title="James Fenimore Cooper">James Fenimore Cooper</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_of_the_Mohicans" title="The Last of the Mohicans">The Last of the Mohicans</a></i>), maps and other printed materials, which testify to how this event held the imagination of the British and North American public long after Wolfe's death in 1759.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/220px-LindsayCambridge.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/330px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/LindsayCambridge.jpg/440px-LindsayCambridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="952" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LindsayCambridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The bombardment of <a href="/wiki/Morro_Castle_(fortress)" title="Morro Castle (fortress)">Morro Castle</a> on <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, 1763</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fantastic_War" title="Fantastic War">Fantastic War</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Cevallos_expedition" title="First Cevallos expedition">First Cevallos expedition</a></div>
<p>In South America (1763), the Portuguese conquered from Spain most of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Negro_(Amazon)" title="Rio Negro (Amazon)">Rio Negro</a> valley,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and repelled a Spanish attack on <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">Mato Grosso</a> (in the <a href="/wiki/Guapor%C3%A9_River" title="Guaporé River">Guaporé River</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between September 1762 and April 1763, Spanish forces led by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Antonio_de_Cevallos" title="Pedro Antonio de Cevallos">don Pedro Antonio de Cevallos</a>, Governor of Buenos Aires (and later first <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_the_Rio_de_la_Plata" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroyalty of the Rio de la Plata">Viceroy of the Rio de la Plata</a>) undertook a campaign against the Portuguese in Uruguay and South Brazil. The Spaniards conquered the Portuguese territories of <a href="/wiki/Colonia_del_Sacramento" title="Colonia del Sacramento">Colonia do Sacramento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande,_Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande, Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande de São Pedro</a> and forced the Portuguese to surrender and retreat.</p>
<p>Under the Treaty of Paris (1763), Spain had to return to Portugal the colony of Sacramento, while the vast and rich territory of the so-called “Continent of S. Peter” (the present day Brazilian state of <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a>) would be retaken from the Spanish army during the undeclared Hispano-Portuguese war of 1763–1777.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bento_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bento-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lesser_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lesser-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bento.2C_Cl.C3.A1udio_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bento.2C_Cl.C3.A1udio-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>As consequence of the war the <a href="/wiki/Valdivian_Fort_System" title="Valdivian Fort System">Valdivian Fort System</a>, a Spanish defensive complex in <a href="/wiki/Zona_Sur" title="Zona Sur">southern Chile</a>, was updated and reinforced from 1764 onwards. Other vulnerable localities of <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Chile" title="Colonial Chile">colonial Chile</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9_Archipelago" title="Chiloé Archipelago">Chiloé Archipelago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n,_Chile" title="Concepción, Chile">Concepción</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Islands" title="Juan Fernández Islands">Juan Fernández Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valparaíso">Valparaíso</a> were also made ready for an eventual English attack.<sup id="cite_ref-MEMCh_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEMCh-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MEMCh2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEMCh2-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Third_Carnatic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Carnatic War">Third Carnatic War</a></div>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Third_Carnatic_War" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
<tr>
<th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_East_Indies" title="Template:Campaignbox Seven Years' War: East Indies"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_East_Indies" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Seven Years' War: East Indies"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_East_Indies&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Third_Carnatic_War" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a href="/wiki/Third_Carnatic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Carnatic War"><span class="wrap">Third Carnatic War</span></a></span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chandannagar" title="Battle of Chandannagar">Chandannagar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Plassey</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cuddalore_(1758)" title="Battle of Cuddalore (1758)">Cuddalore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Negapatam_(1758)" title="Battle of Negapatam (1758)">Negapatam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Condore" title="Battle of Condore">Condore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Madras" title="Siege of Madras">Madras</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Masulipatam" title="Siege of Masulipatam">Masulipatam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pondicherry" title="Battle of Pondicherry">Battle of Pondicherry</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chinsurah" title="Battle of Chinsurah">Chinsurah</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wandiwash" title="Battle of Wandiwash">Wandiwash</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pondicherry_(1760)" title="Siege of Pondicherry (1760)">Pondicherry Siege</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>In India, the outbreak of the Seven Years' War in Europe renewed the long running conflict between the French and the British trading companies for influence. The war spread beyond Southern India and into <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a>, where British forces under <a href="/wiki/Robert_Clive" title="Robert Clive">Robert Clive</a> recaptured <a href="/wiki/Calcutta" class="mw-redirect" title="Calcutta">Calcutta</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Nawab" title="Nawab">Nawab</a> <a href="/wiki/Siraj_ud-Daulah" title="Siraj ud-Daulah">Siraj ud-Daulah</a>, a French ally, and ousted him from his throne at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plassey" title="Battle of Plassey">Battle of Plassey</a> in 1757. In the same year, the British also captured the French settlement in Bengal at <a href="/wiki/Chandernagar" class="mw-redirect" title="Chandernagar">Chandernagar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the south, although the French captured <a href="/wiki/Cuddalore" title="Cuddalore">Cuddalore</a>, their <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Madras" title="Siege of Madras">siege of Madras</a> failed, while the British commander <a href="/wiki/Sir_Eyre_Coote" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Eyre Coote">Sir Eyre Coote</a> decisively defeated the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Arthur,_comte_de_Lally" title="Thomas Arthur, comte de Lally">Comte de Lally</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wandiwash" title="Battle of Wandiwash">Battle of Wandiwash</a> in 1760 and overran the French territory of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Circars" title="Northern Circars">Northern Circars</a>. The French capital of <a href="/wiki/Puducherry" title="Puducherry">Pondicherry</a> fell to the British in 1761; together with the fall of the lesser French settlements of <a href="/wiki/Karikal" class="mw-redirect" title="Karikal">Karikal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahé, India">Mahé</a> this effectively eliminated French power in India.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Africa">West Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: West Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Seven_Years.27_War:West_Africa_Campaign" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
<tr>
<th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_Africa" title="Template:Campaignbox Seven Years' War: Africa"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_Africa" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Seven Years' War: Africa"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_Africa&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none;">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Seven_Years.27_War:West_Africa_Campaign" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a class="mw-selflink selflink"><span class="wrap">Seven Years' War</span></a>:<br />
West Africa Campaign</span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Senegal" title="Capture of Senegal">Senegal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gor%C3%A9e" title="Capture of Gorée">Gorée</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_expedition_against_the_Gambia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="British expedition against the Gambia (page does not exist)">Gambia</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>In 1758, at the urging of an American merchant, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cumming" title="Thomas Cumming">Thomas Cumming</a>, Pitt dispatched an expedition to take the French settlement at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis,_Senegal" title="Saint-Louis, Senegal">Saint Louis</a>. The British <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Senegal" title="Capture of Senegal">captured Senegal</a> with ease in May 1758 and brought home large amounts of captured goods. This success convinced Pitt to launch two further expeditions to take the island of <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée</a> and the French trading post on <a href="/wiki/River_Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="River Gambia">the Gambia</a>. The loss of these valuable colonies further weakened the French economy.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outcome">Outcome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Outcome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" width="38" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:
<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a></b></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Anglo-French hostilities were ended in 1763 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>, which involved a complex series of land exchanges, the most important being France's cession to Spain of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a>, and to Great Britain the rest of New France except for the islands of <a href="/wiki/St._Pierre_and_Miquelon" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Pierre and Miquelon">St. Pierre and Miquelon</a>. Faced with the choice of regaining either <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> or its Caribbean island colonies of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guadeloupe" title="History of Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Martinique" title="History of Martinique">Martinique</a>, France chose the latter to retain these lucrative sources of sugar,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> writing off New France as an unproductive, costly territory.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> France also returned Menorca to the British. Spain lost control of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a> to Great Britain, but it received from the French the <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans,_Louisiana" title="Île d'Orléans, Louisiana">Île d'Orléans</a> and all of the former French holdings west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. The exchanges suited the British as well, as their own Caribbean islands already supplied ample sugar, and, with the acquisition of New France and Florida, they now controlled all of North America east of the Mississippi.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vorderlader.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vorderlader.jpg/210px-Vorderlader.jpg" width="210" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vorderlader.jpg/315px-Vorderlader.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Vorderlader.jpg/420px-Vorderlader.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vorderlader.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historical re-enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Warburg" title="Battle of Warburg">Battle of Warburg</a> fought on 31 July 1760</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In India, the British retained the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Circars" title="Northern Circars">Northern Circars</a>, but returned all the French trading ports. The treaty, however, required that the fortifications of these settlements be destroyed and never rebuilt, while only minimal garrisons could be maintained there, thus rendering them worthless as military bases. Combined with the loss of France's ally in <a href="/wiki/Nawab_of_Bengal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nawab of Bengal">Bengal</a> and the defection of <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad state">Hyderabad</a> to the British as a result of the war, this effectively brought French power in India to an end, making way for <a href="/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India" title="Presidencies and provinces of British India">British hegemony</a> and eventual control of the subcontinent.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> France's navy was crippled by the war. Only after an ambitious rebuilding program in combination with Spain was France again able to challenge Britain's command of the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bute’s settlement with France was mild compared with what Pitt’s would have been. He had hoped for a lasting peace with France, and he was afraid that if he took too much, the whole of Europe would unite in envious hostility against Great Britain. Choiseul, however, had no intention of making a permanent peace, and, when France went to war with Great Britain during the American Revolution, the British found no support among the European powers.<sup id="cite_ref-Eric_Robson_1957_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eric_Robson_1957-118">[118]</a></sup> France's defeat caused the French to embark upon major military reforms, with particular attention being paid to the artillery.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> The origins of the <a href="/wiki/Gribeauval_system" title="Gribeauval system">famed French artillery</a> that played a prominent role in the wars of the French Revolutionary wars and beyond can to be traced to military reforms that started in 1763.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Treaty of Hubertusburg, between Austria, Prussia, and Saxony, was signed on 15 February 1763, at a hunting lodge between <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>. Negotiations had started there on 31 December 1762. Frederick, who had considered ceding East Prussia to Russia if Peter III helped him secure Saxony, finally insisted on excluding Russia (in fact, no longer a belligerent) from the negotiations. At the same time, he refused to evacuate Saxony until its elector had renounced any claim to reparation. The Austrians wanted at least to retain <a href="/wiki/Glatz" class="mw-disambig" title="Glatz">Glatz</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint Inline-Template" style="vertical-align:text-top;white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dispenser.homenet.org/~dispenser/cgi-bin/dab_solver.py?page=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;editintro=Template:Disambiguation_needed/editintro&amp;client=Template:Dn"><span title="Link needs disambiguation. (January 2017)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, which they had in fact reconquered, but Frederick would not allow it. The treaty simply restored the status quo of 1748, with Silesia and Glatz reverting to Frederick and Saxony to its own elector. The only concession that Prussia made to Austria was to consent to the election of Archduke Joseph as Holy Roman emperor.</p>
<p>Austria was not able to retake Silesia or make any significant territorial gain. However, it did prevent Prussia from invading parts of Saxony. More significantly, its military performance proved far better than during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> and seemed to vindicate Maria Theresa's administrative and military reforms. Hence, Austria's prestige was restored in great part and the empire secured its position as a major player in the European system.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Also, by promising to vote for Joseph II in the Imperial elections, Frederick II accepted the Habsburg preeminence in the Holy Roman Empire. The survival of Prussia as a first-rate power and the enhanced prestige of its king and its army, however, was potentially damaging in the long run to Austria's influence in Germany.</p>
<p>Not only that, Austria now found herself estranged with the new developments within the empire itself. Beside the rise of Prussia, <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus III">Augustus III</a>, although ineffective, could muster an army not only from Saxony, but also Poland, since he was also the King of Poland as well as Elector of Saxony. Bavaria's growing power and independence was also apparent as it asserted more control on the deployment of its army, and managed to disengage from the war at its own will. Most importantly, with the now belligerent Hanover united personally under <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="George III of Great Britain">George III of Great Britain</a>, It amassed a considerable power, and even brought Britain in, on future conflicts. This power dynamic was important to the future and the latter conflicts of the <i>Reich</i>. The war also proved that Maria Theresa's reforms were still insufficient to compete with Prussia: unlike its enemy, the Austrians were almost bankrupt at the end of war. Hence, she dedicated the next two decades to the consolidation of her administration.</p>
<p>Prussia emerged from the war as a great power whose importance could no longer be challenged. Frederick the Great’s personal reputation was enormously enhanced, as his debt to fortune (Russia’s volte-face after Elizabeth’s death) and to British financial support were soon forgotten, while the memory of his energy and his military genius was strenuously kept alive.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> Though depicted as a key moment in Prussia's rise to greatness, the war weakened Prussia.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> Prussia's lands and population were devastated, though Frederick's extensive agrarian reforms and encouragement of immigration soon solved both these problems. Unfortunately for Prussia, its army had taken heavy losses (particularly the officer corps), and in the war's aftermath, Frederick could not afford to rebuild the Prussian Army to what it was before the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> In the War of the Bavarian Succession, the Prussians fought poorly despite being led by Frederick in person.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> During the war with France in 1792–1795, the Prussian Army did not fare well against revolutionary France, and in 1806, the Prussians were annihilated by the French at the Battle of Jena.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> It was only after 1806 when Prussian government brought in reforms to recover from the disaster of Jena that Prussia's rise to greatness later in the 19th century was realized.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> However, none of this had happened yet, and after 1763, various nations all sent officers to Prussia to learn the secrets of Prussia's military power.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> After the Seven Years' War, Prussia become one of the most imitated powers in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Russia, on the other hand, made one great invisible gain from the war: the elimination of French influence in Poland. The <a href="/wiki/First_Partition_of_Poland" title="First Partition of Poland">First Partition of Poland</a> (1772) was to be a Russo-Prussian transaction, with Austria only reluctantly involved and with France simply ignored.<sup id="cite_ref-Eric_Robson_1957_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eric_Robson_1957-118">[118]</a></sup> Though the war had ended in a draw, the performance of the Imperial Russian Army against Prussia had improved Russia's reputation as a factor in European politics, as many had not expected the Russians to hold their own against the Prussians in campaigns fought on Prussian soil.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90_119-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_page_90-119">[119]</a></sup> The American historian David Stone observed that Russian soldiers proved capable of going head-on against the Prussians, inflicting and taking one bloody volley after another "without flinching", and though the quality of Russian generalship was quite variable, the Russians were never decisively defeated once in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-121">[121]</a></sup> The Russians defeated the Prussians several times in the war, but the Russians lacked the necessary logistical capability to follow up their victories with lasting gains, and in this sense, the salvation of the House of Hohenzollern was due more to Russian weakness with respect to logistics than to Prussian strength on the battlefield.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Still, the fact that the Russians proved capable of defeating in battle the army of a "first-rate" European power on its own soil despite the often indifferent quality of their generals improved Russia's standing in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-121">[121]</a></sup> A lasting legacy of the war was that it awakened the Russians to their logistic weaknesses, and led to major reforms of the Imperial Russian Army's quartermaster department.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_90-91_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_90-91-123">[123]</a></sup> The supply system that allowed the Russians to advance into the Balkans during the war with the Ottomans in 1787–92, Marshal Alexander Suvorov to campaign effectively in Italy and Switzerland in 1798–99, and for the Russians to fight across Germany and France in 1813–14 to take Paris was created directly in response to the logistic problems experienced by the Russians in the Seven Years' War.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_90-91_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_90-91-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British government was close to bankruptcy, and Britain now faced the delicate task of pacifying its new French-Canadian subjects as well as the many American Indian tribes who had supported France. In 1763, <a href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_War" title="Pontiac's War">Pontiac's War</a> broke out as a group of Indian tribes in the Great Lakes region and the Northwest (the modern American Midwest) said to have been led by the Ottawa chief Pontiac (whose role as the leader of the confederation seems to have been exaggerated by the British), unhappy with the eclipse of French power, rebelled against British rule. The Indians had long established congenial and friendly relations with the French fur traders, and the Anglo-American fur traders who had replaced the French had engaged in business practices that enraged the Indians, who complained about being cheated when they sold their furs.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_84-85_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_84-85-124">[124]</a></sup> Moreover, the Indians feared that with the coming of British rule might lead to white settlers displacing them off their land, whereas it was known that the French had only come as fur traders.<sup id="cite_ref-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_84-85_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marston.2C_Daniel_pages_84-85-124">[124]</a></sup> Pontiac's War was a major conflict in which the British temporarily lost control of the Great Lakes-Northwest regions to the Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> By the middle of 1763, the only forts the British held in the region were Fort Detroit (modern Detroit, Michigan ), Fort Niagara (modern Youngstown, New York) and Fort Pitt (modern Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania) with the rest all being lost to the Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> It was only with the British victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bushy_Run" title="Battle of Bushy Run">Battle of Bushy Run</a> that prevented a complete collapse of British power in the Great Lakes region.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> King George&#160;III's <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_1763" class="mw-redirect" title="Proclamation of 1763">Proclamation of 1763</a>, which forbade white settlement beyond the crest of the Appalachians, was intended to appease the Indians but led to considerable outrage in the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>, whose inhabitants were eager to acquire native lands. The <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">Quebec Act</a> of 1774, similarly intended to win over the loyalty of French Canadians, also spurred resentment among American colonists.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The act protected Catholic religion and French language, which enraged the Americans, but the Québécois remained loyal to the British Crown during the American Revolution and did not rebel.</p>
<p>The war also brought to an end the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">"Old System" of alliances in Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-os_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os-129">[129]</a></sup> In the years after the war, under the direction of <a href="/wiki/John_Montagu,_4th_Earl_of_Sandwich" title="John Montagu, 4th Earl of Sandwich">Lord Sandwich</a>, the British attempted to re-establish this system. But after her surprising grand success against a coalition of great powers, European states such as Austria, The Dutch Republic, Sweden, Denmark-Norway, Ottoman Empire, and Russia now saw Britain as a greater threat than France and did not join them, while the Prussians were angered by what they considered a British betrayal in 1762. Consequently, when the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a> turned into a global war between 1778–83, Britain found itself opposed by a strong coalition of European powers, and lacking any substantial ally.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_references">Cultural references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cultural references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Luck_of_Barry_Lyndon" title="The Luck of Barry Lyndon">The Luck of Barry Lyndon</a></i> (1844) by <a href="/wiki/William_Makepeace_Thackeray" title="William Makepeace Thackeray">William Makepeace Thackeray</a> is set against the Seven Years' War. This is a quote about the war from the novel:
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It would require a greater philosopher and historian than I am to explain the causes of the famous Seven Years' War in which Europe was engaged; and, indeed, its origin has always appeared to me to be so complicated, and the books written about it so amazingly hard to understand, that I have seldom been much wiser at the end of a chapter than at the beginning, and so shall not trouble my reader with any personal disquisitions concerning the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Barry_Lyndon" title="Barry Lyndon">Barry Lyndon</a></i> (1975) is based on the Thackeray novel.</li>
<li>The events in the early chapters of Voltaire's <i><a href="/wiki/Candide" title="Candide">Candide</a></i> are based on the Seven Years' War; according to <a href="/wiki/Jean_Starobinski" title="Jean Starobinski">Jean Starobinski</a>, ("Voltaire's Double-Barreled Musket", in <i>Blessings In Disguise</i> (California, 1993) p.&#160;85), all the atrocities described in Chapter&#160;3 are true to life. When <i>Candide</i> was written, <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> had been opposed to <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">militarism</a>; the book's themes of disillusionment and suffering underscore this position</li>
<li>The board games <i><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_(board_game)" title="Friedrich (board game)">Friedrich</a></i> and, more recently, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prussia%27s_Defiant_Stand_(board_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Prussia's Defiant Stand (board game) (page does not exist)">Prussia's Defiant Stand</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clash_of_Monarchs_(board_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clash of Monarchs (board game) (page does not exist)">Clash of Monarchs</a></i> are based on the events of the Seven Years' War</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_strategy_wargame" title="Grand strategy wargame">Grand strategy wargame</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Prussia" title="Rise of Prussia">Rise of Prussia</a></i> covers the European campaigns of the Seven Years' War</li>
<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_of_the_Mohicans" title="The Last of the Mohicans">The Last of the Mohicans</a></i> (1826) by <a href="/wiki/James_Fenimore_Cooper" title="James Fenimore Cooper">James Fenimore Cooper</a> and its subsequent adaptations are set in the Northern American Theatre of the Seven Years' War</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Partisan_in_War" title="The Partisan in War">The Partisan in War</a></i> (1789), a treatise on light infantry tactics written by <a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">Colonel</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andreas_Emmerich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Andreas Emmerich (page does not exist)">Andreas Emmerich</a>, is based on his experiences in the Seven Years' War.</li>
<li>The Seven Years' War is the central theme of <a href="/wiki/Gotthold_Ephraim_Lessing" title="Gotthold Ephraim Lessing">G.&#160;E. Lessing's</a> 1767 play <i><a href="/wiki/Minna_von_Barnhelm" title="Minna von Barnhelm">Minna von Barnhelm or the Soldiers' Happiness</a></i>.</li>
<li>Numerous towns and other places now in United States were named after <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> to commemorate the victorious conclusion of the war, including <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Maryland" title="Frederick, Maryland">Frederick</a>, Maryland, and <a href="/wiki/King_of_Prussia,_Pennsylvania" title="King of Prussia, Pennsylvania">King of Prussia</a>, Pennsylvania.</li>
<li>The fourth scenario of the second act in the <a href="/wiki/Real-time_strategy" title="Real-time strategy">RTS</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Age_of_Empires_III" title="Age of Empires III">Age of Empires&#160;III</a></i> is about this military conflict, with the player fighting alongside the French against the British.</li>
<li>In Ubisoft's video game <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_III" title="Assassin's Creed III">Assassin's Creed III</a></i>, early missions in the main story/campaign centred around the Assassin/Templar Haytham Kenway are set during the North American campaigns of the French and Indian War. Additionally, the prequel <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_Rogue" title="Assassin's Creed Rogue">Assassin's Creed Rogue</a></i>, released in 2014, is set within the timescale of the Seven Years' War.</li>
<li>Several installments of <a href="/wiki/Diana_Gabaldon" title="Diana Gabaldon">Diana Gabaldon</a>'s fictional <a href="/wiki/Lord_John_series" title="Lord John series"><i>Lord John</i> series</a> (itself an offshoot of the <a href="/wiki/Outlander_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Outlander series"><i>Outlander</i> series</a>) describe a homosexual officer's experiences in Germany and France during the Seven Years' War. In particular, the short story "Lord John and the Succubus" occurs just before the Battle of Rossbach, and the novel <i>Lord John and the Brotherhood of the Blade</i> centers around the Battle of Krefeld.</li>
</ul>
